  1. Global Legal Document Taxonomy

  Primary Categories (18 Document Types)

  LEGAL DOCUMENT UNIVERSE
  │
  ├── 1. JUDICIAL DOCUMENTS
  │   ├── Judgments/Decisions (your current focus)
  │   ├── Court Orders (interim, procedural)
  │   ├── Judicial Opinions (majority, concurring, dissenting)
  │   └── Judicial Notices & Circulars
  │
  ├── 2. LEGISLATIVE DOCUMENTS
  │   ├── Primary Legislation (Acts, Statutes, Codes)
  │   ├── Bills & Draft Laws (pending legislation)
  │   ├── Amendments (modifications to existing laws)
  │   └── Legislative History (debates, committee reports)
  │

  │   ├── Regulations & Rules (executive/administrative)
  │   ├── Directives & Circulars (government instructions)

  │

  │   ├── Constitutions (national, state/provincial)
  │   ├── Constitutional Amendments
  │   └── Basic Laws & Charters
  │
  ├── 5. CONTRACTUAL DOCUMENTS
  │   ├── Commercial Contracts (sale, service, employment)
  │   ├── Real Estate Documents (deeds, leases, mortgages)
  │   ├── Loan Agreements & Financial Instruments
  │   └── MoUs & Letters of Intent

  ├── 6. INTERNATIONAL LAW
  │   ├── Treaties & Conventions (bilateral, multilateral)

  │   ├── International Court Decisions (ICJ, ICC, etc.)
  │   └── UN Resolutions & Declarations
  │
  ├── 7. PROCEDURAL DOCUMENTS
  │   ├── Pleadings (complaints, answers, replies)
  │   ├── Motions & Applications
  │   ├── Briefs & Written Arguments
  │   └── Affidavits & Declarations
  │
  ├── 8. LEGAL OPINIONS & COMMENTARY
  │   ├── Attorney General Opinions
  │   ├── Legal Memoranda (internal analysis)
  │   ├── Law Review Articles (scholarly)
  │   └── Practice Guides & Commentaries
  │
  └── 9. ADMINISTRATIVE DOCUMENTS
      ├── Government Orders & Notifications
      ├── Licensing & Permits
      ├── Regulatory Filings

  ---
  2. Structural Analysis by Document Type

  Key Structural Differences:

  | Document Type | Primary Structure      | Granularity Units                     | Avg Length     | Reference Density        |
  |---------------|------------------------|---------------------------------------|----------------|--------------------------|
  | Judgments     | Narrative + Analytical | Sections (Facts, Holdings, etc.)      | 5K-50K words   | High (15-50 citations)   |
  | Statutes      | Hierarchical           | Part → Chapter → Section → Subsection | 10K-200K words | Medium (cross-refs)      |
  | Regulations   | Rule-Based             | Rule → Clause → Sub-clause            | 2K-50K words   | High (statute refs)      |
  | Contracts     | Clause-Based           | Article → Clause → Paragraph          | 2K-20K words   | Low (boilerplate)        |
  | Treaties      | Protocol-Based         | Preamble → Article → Protocol → Annex | 5K-100K words  | Medium (intl law)        |
  | Bills         | Section-Based          | Title → Part → Section → Amendment    | 5K-50K words   | Medium (existing law)    |
  | Pleadings     | Argument-Based         | Claims → Facts → Legal Basis → Prayer | 2K-15K words   | Medium (case law)        |
  | Opinions      | Analytical             | Issue → Analysis → Conclusion         | 3K-30K words   | Very High (40-100 cites) |

  Critical Insight:

  - Judgments: Narrative flow (facts → reasoning → decision)
  - Statutes: Hierarchical tree (nested sections)
  - Contracts: Standalone clauses (each clause independent)
  - Treaties: Multi-lingual parallel texts (alignment challenge)

  ---
  3. Universal Chunk Type Schema

  Problem with Current 8 Types:

  Your current schema is judgment-centric:
  - facts, holding, reasoning, dissent → Only applicable to judgments
  - statute_interpretation → Only when judgment interprets statute
  - Doesn't cover: contract clauses, statutory provisions, treaty articles, etc.

  Proposed Universal Schema: 16 Core Chunk Types

      {"name": "dissent", "scope": "judgments", "priority": "low"},
      {"name": "procedural_history", "scope": "judgments", "priority": "low"},

      {"name": "statute_interpretation", "scope": "judgments, opinions", "priority": "high"}

  ---
  4. Document-Specific Chunking Strategies

  A. Statutes & Codes (Hierarchical Chunking)

  Challenge: Nested structure creates context dependency
  Income Tax Act, 1961
  ├── Part A: General
  │   ├── Chapter I: Preliminary
  │   │   ├── Section 1: Short title, extent, commencement
  │   │   ├── Section 2: Definitions
  │   │   │   ├── (1) "Assessee" means...
  │   │   │   ├── (14) "Capital asset" means...
  │   │   │   └── (45) "Transfer" means...
  │   │   └── Section 3: Previous year defined
  │   └── Chapter II: Basis of charge
  └── Part B: Computation of Total Income
      └── (1000+ sections)

  Recommended Strategy: Contextual Hierarchical Chunking
  APPROACH 1: Section-Level with Context Injection
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Chunk Structure:
    Metadata Header:
      Act: Income Tax Act, 1961
      Part: A - General
      Chapter: I - Preliminary
      Section: 2(14)

    Chunk Text:
      "2. Definitions.
       (14) 'Capital asset' means property of any kind held by an assessee,
       whether or not connected with his business or profession, but does
       not include—
       (i) any stock-in-trade...
       (ii) movable property..."

    Size: 150-600 tokens per section/subsection
    Type: legislative_provision OR definition (if definitional section)

  APPROACH 2: Multi-Level Chunking (Recommended)
  ───────────────────────────────────────────────
  Level 1: Section Summary Chunk (for broad retrieval)
    - "Section 2(14) defines 'Capital asset' excluding stock-in-trade,
       personal effects under ₹3 lakhs, agricultural land, etc."
    - Size: 50-150 tokens
    - Type: definition

  Level 2: Full Section Chunk (for detailed retrieval)
    - Complete section text with all subsections
    - Size: 200-800 tokens
    - Type: legislative_provision

  Level 3: Proviso/Exception Chunks (for edge cases)
    - Extract "Provided that..." clauses separately
    - Size: 100-300 tokens
    - Type: exception_proviso

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Section level (NOT subsection, too granular)
  - Size: 200-600 tokens (statutes are dense)
  - Overlap: 0 tokens (sections are standalone)
  - Metadata: Act name, Part, Chapter, Section number, Amendment history

  ---
  B. Contracts & Agreements (Clause-Based Chunking)

  Challenge: Clauses reference each other, boilerplate vs custom clauses

  Recommended Strategy: Semantic Clause Chunking
  CHUNKING RULES:
  ─────────────────
  1. One clause = One chunk (clauses are atomic units)
  2. Classify clause type automatically:
     - obligation_clause: "Party A shall..."
     - condition_clause: "Upon the occurrence of..."
     - representation_warranty: "Party B represents that..."
     - remedy_clause: "In the event of breach..."
     - definition: "'Effective Date' means..."

  3. Prepend contract metadata:
     Contract: Software License Agreement
     Parties: Licensor (Company A) & Licensee (Company B)
     Date: 2024-01-15
     Clause: 5.3 - Termination Rights

  4. Extract cross-references:
     "...as defined in Clause 3.1..." → Create relationship to Clause 3.1

  5. De-duplicate boilerplate:
     - Generic clauses (force majeure, governing law) → Lower priority
     - Custom clauses → Higher priority

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Clause level (Article 5 → Clause 5.1, 5.2, 5.3)
  - Size: 100-500 tokens per clause
  - Overlap: 0 (clauses independent)
  - Type Detection: LLM-based classification into 4 contract chunk types

  ---
  C. Treaties & International Law (Protocol-Based + Multi-Lingual)

  Challenge: Multiple language versions, complex protocol structure

  Recommended Strategy: Parallel Text Chunking
  STRUCTURE:
  ──────────
  Paris Agreement on Climate Change
  ├── Preamble (chunk separately)
  ├── Article 1: Definitions (chunk by definition)
  ├── Article 2: Goals (chunk as treaty_article)
  ├── Article 3: Contributions (chunk with NDC context)
  ├── ...
  ├── Article 29: Entry into force (procedural)
  └── Annexes (chunk separately)

  MULTI-LINGUAL HANDLING:
  ───────────────────────
  Chunk ID: paris_agreement_art2_en
  Parallel Chunks:
    - paris_agreement_art2_fr (French authentic text)
    - paris_agreement_art2_es (Spanish authentic text)
    - paris_agreement_art2_zh (Chinese authentic text)

  Link via relationship: TRANSLATION_OF

  EMBEDDING STRATEGY:
  ───────────────────
  Option 1: Embed each language separately (BGE-M3 supports 100+ languages)
  Option 2: Embed English + store other languages as metadata

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Article level
  - Size: 150-600 tokens
  - Type: treaty_article (primary), definition (Article 1), international_principle

  ---
  D. Regulations & Rules (Rule-Based Chunking)

  Challenge: Dense sub-clauses, frequent amendments

  Recommended Strategy: Rule-Level with Amendment Tracking
  EXAMPLE: GDPR Article 6 (Lawfulness of processing)
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Chunk 1:
    Doc: GDPR (EU 2016/679)
    Article: 6
    Type: regulatory_rule

    "Processing shall be lawful only if at least one of the following applies:
     (a) the data subject has given consent...
     (b) processing is necessary for contract performance...
     (c) processing is necessary for compliance with legal obligation..."

    Size: 400 tokens

  Chunk 2 (Exception):
    Doc: GDPR (EU 2016/679)
    Article: 6(1)(f)
    Type: exception_proviso

    "Legitimate interests pursued by controller, except where overridden
     by interests of data subject, particularly if data subject is a child."

    Size: 150 tokens
    Amendment: None
    Related: Article 7 (Consent conditions)

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Rule/Sub-rule level
  - Size: 150-600 tokens
  - Overlap: 0
  - Amendment Tracking: Store version history in changelog

  ---
  E. Pleadings & Briefs (Argument-Based Chunking)

  Challenge: Persuasive narrative structure, heavy citations

  Recommended Strategy: Claim-Based Chunking
  STRUCTURE:
  ──────────
  Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus
  ├── Caption (metadata only, don't chunk)
  ├── Introduction (chunk as: arguments, 200 tokens)
  ├── Statement of Facts (chunk as: facts, 500-1000 tokens)
  ├── Legal Arguments
  │   ├── Argument I: Violation of Article 21
  │   │   ├── Sub-argument A: Arbitrary detention (chunk: arguments, 400 tokens)
  │   │   └── Sub-argument B: Precedent analysis (chunk: precedent_discussion, 300 tokens)
  │   ├── Argument II: Procedural irregularity
  │   │   └── (chunk as: procedural_history + arguments)
  │   └── Argument III: Constitutional remedy
  │       └── (chunk as: legal_analysis)
  └── Prayer/Relief Sought (metadata only)

  CITATION HANDLING:
  ──────────────────
  "As held in Maneka Gandhi v. Union of India (1978) 1 SCC 248, Article 21
   encompasses procedural fairness..."

  → Extract citation: Create CITES relationship to Maneka Gandhi case
  → Keep citation in chunk text (preserve context)

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Argument level
  - Size: 300-800 tokens per argument
  - Type: arguments (primary), legal_analysis, precedent_discussion

  7. Neo4j Schema Expansion

  New Node Types Needed (Beyond Current 24):

  // Legislative nodes
  CREATE (s:Statute {statute_id, title, jurisdiction, enactment_date})
  CREATE (sec:Section {section_id, section_number, parent_statute})
  CREATE (a:Amendment {amendment_id, amendment_date, amending_act})

  // Contractual nodes
  CREATE (c:Contract {contract_id, parties, execution_date})
  CREATE (cl:Clause {clause_id, clause_number, clause_type})

  // International law nodes
  CREATE (t:Treaty {treaty_id, treaty_name, adoption_date})
  CREATE (p:Protocol {protocol_id, parent_treaty})

  // Regulatory nodes
  CREATE (r:Regulation {regulation_id, issuing_authority})

  New Relationships:

  // Legislative relationships
  (:Judgment)-[:INTERPRETS]->(:Section)
  (:Statute)-[:AMENDED_BY]->(:Amendment)
  (:Section)-[:PART_OF]->(:Statute)
  (:Regulation)-[:IMPLEMENTS]->(:Statute)

  // Contractual relationships
  (:Contract)-[:CONTAINS_CLAUSE]->(:Clause)
  (:Clause)-[:REFERENCES_CLAUSE]->(:Clause)
  (:Contract)-[:GOVERNED_BY]->(:Statute)

  // International relationships
  (:Treaty)-[:HAS_PROTOCOL]->(:Protocol)
  (:Judgment)-[:APPLIES_TREATY]->(:Treaty)
  (:Statute)-[:IMPLEMENTS_TREATY]->(:Treaty)

  Phase 1: Core Legal Documents (60% of queries)

  Priority 1A: Judgments ✅ (Already designed)
  Priority 1B: Statutes & Codes (35% of queries)
  Priority 1C: Regulations (15% of queries)

  Phase 2: Transactional Documents (25% of queries)

  Priority 2A: Contracts & Agreements

  Phase 3: Specialized Documents (15% of queries)

  9. Universal Chunking Pipeline (Revised)

  INPUT: Any legal document (judgment, statute, contract, treaty, etc.)
      ↓
  STEP 1: Document Classification
      - Detect document type using LLM + rule-based heuristics
      - Keywords: "JUDGMENT", "ACT", "AGREEMENT", "TREATY", etc.
      - Structure patterns: Numbered sections, clause structure, etc.
      ↓
  STEP 2: Extract Document-Specific Metadata
      - Judgments → court, judges, citation, date
      - Statutes → act name, chapter, section, amendment history
      - Contracts → parties, execution date, governing law
      - Treaties → treaty name, parties, adoption date, language
      ↓
  STEP 3: Apply Document-Specific Chunking Strategy
      ┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
      │ IF document_type == "judgment":         │
      │   → Use semantic section chunking       │
      │   → Chunk types: holding, reasoning, etc│
      │                                         │
      │ ELIF document_type == "statute":        │
      │   → Use hierarchical section chunking   │
      │   → Chunk types: legislative_provision  │
      │                                         │
      │ ELIF document_type == "contract":       │
      │   → Use clause-based chunking           │
      │   → Chunk types: obligation_clause, etc │
      │                                         │
      │ ELIF document_type == "treaty":         │
      │   → Use article-based chunking          │
      │   → Chunk types: treaty_article         │
      └─────────────────────────────────────────┘
      ↓
  STEP 4: Chunk Type Classification
      - LLM classifies each chunk into 16 universal types
      - Uses keywords + context + document type
      ↓
  STEP 5: Cross-Reference Extraction
      - Extract citations: "Section 22A", "Article 32", "Clause 5.3"
      - Create Neo4j relationships: CITES, REFERENCES, INTERPRETS
      ↓
  STEP 6: Metadata Enrichment & Embedding
      - Prepend context: doc type + metadata + chunk type
      - Generate embeddings (BGE-M3)
      - Calculate trust_score, confidence_score
      ↓
  OUTPUT: Universal chunks ready for Neo4j + Weaviate indexing

  ---
  10. Retrieval Strategy Adaptations

  Query → Document Type Routing

  QUERY ANALYSIS:
  ───────────────
  "What is the penalty for data breach?"
  → Document types: statutes (GDPR), regulations (data protection rules)
  → Chunk types: regulatory_rule, remedy_clause
  → Boost: legislative_provision chunks with "penalty", "fine", "sanction"

  "Show me force majeure clauses"
  → Document types: contracts
  → Chunk types: condition_clause
  → Boost: contract chunks with keywords "force majeure", "act of god"

  "Cases interpreting Article 21"
  → Document types: judgments
  → Chunk types: statute_interpretation, legal_analysis
  → Boost: chunks with "Article 21" + "held" + "Constitution"

  "Treaty obligations on climate finance"
  → Document types: treaties
  → Chunk types: treaty_article, obligation_clause
  → Boost: treaty chunks with "climate", "finance", "developed countries"

  Multi-Document Retrieval Pipeline

  STAGE 1: Identify Relevant Document Types
      Query: "GDPR consent requirements in employment contracts"
      → Document types: regulations (GDPR) + contracts (employment)
      ↓
  STAGE 2: Parallel Retrieval Across Document Types
      Path A: Search regulations for "consent" → regulatory_rule chunks
      Path B: Search contracts for "consent" → obligation_clause chunks
      Path C: Search judgments for "GDPR employment consent" → legal_analysis
      ↓
  STAGE 3: Cross-Document Fusion
      - Merge results using RRF
      - Boost chunks with cross-references (contract referencing GDPR)
      - Rank by: similarity (0.4) + trust_score (0.3) + document_type_relevance (0.3)
      ↓
  OUTPUT: Top 10 chunks across multiple document types

  11. Final Recommendations

  Immediate Actions:

  1. Expand Chunk Type Schema to 16 Types
    - Add 8 new types: legislative_provision, regulatory_rule, definition, exception_proviso, obligation_clause, condition_clause, treaty_article, procedural_rule
    - Keep your existing 8 judgment types
  2. Implement Document Type Detection
    - LLM-based classifier to detect 18 document types
    - Rule-based heuristics for common patterns
  3. Create Document-Specific Chunking Pipelines
    - Priority 1: Statutes (hierarchical chunking)
    - Priority 2: Contracts (clause-based chunking)
    - Priority 3: Regulations (rule-based chunking)
  4. Expand Neo4j Schema
    - Add nodes: Statute, Section, Contract, Clause, Treaty
    - Add relationships: INTERPRETS, IMPLEMENTS, REFERENCES
  5. Update Retrieval Logic
    - Query → document type routing
    - Multi-document type fusion
    - Document-type-aware reranking

  Quality Targets for Universal System:

  | Metric                           | Target | Measurement                             |
  |----------------------------------|--------|-----------------------------------------|
  | Document Type Detection Accuracy | >95%   | Auto-classification of 18 types         |
  | Chunk Type Classification        | >90%   | Correct assignment of 16 types          |
  | Cross-Document Retrieval         | >85%   | Relevant chunks from multiple doc types |
  | Citation Extraction              | >95%   | Complete citations preserved            |
  | Multilingual Support (Treaties)  | >90%   | Parallel text alignment                 |

  CRITICAL FINDINGS

  1. Coverage Gap: Only 29% Complete

  Your current 21-type taxonomy covers less than one-third of essential legal documents needed for a universal legal RAG system.

  2. Major Missing Categories (52 Document Types)

  Criminal Law (8 types): FIRs, charge sheets, arrest warrants, search warrants, bail orders, conviction/acquittal orders
  Corporate Law (9 types): Articles of association, shareholder agreements, prospectuses, IPO documents, board resolutions, M&A agreements
  Intellectual Property (7 types): Patent applications/grants, trademark/copyright registrations, IP licensing, oppositions
  Family Law (6 types): Divorce decrees, custody orders, adoption orders, maintenance orders, prenuptial agreements
  Tax Law (6 types): Assessment orders, demand notices, advance rulings, appeal orders
  Alternative Dispute Resolution (3 types): Arbitration awards, mediation settlements, conciliation agreements
  Plus 13 more specialized categories

  3. Jurisdictional Gaps

  - Common Law: Missing UK, US, Australia, Canada, Singapore coverage
  - Civil Law: Zero coverage (France, Germany, Japan, Latin America)
  - Islamic Law: Zero coverage (Saudi Arabia, UAE, Malaysia, Indonesia)
  - Hybrid Systems: Zero coverage (South Africa, Scotland, Israel)

  4. Chunk Type Deficiencies

  Your current 8 chunk types (optimized for judgments) cannot handle:
  - Statutory sections and provisos
  - Contract clauses and conditions
  - Patent claims and technical descriptions
  - Tax computations and financial tables
  - Environmental impact assessments
  - Criminal procedure documents

  27 new chunk types required for comprehensive coverage.

  PROPOSED SOLUTION: 73-Type Universal Taxonomy

  The evaluation recommends expanding from 21 to 73 document types organized into:

  Category A: Judicial Documents (15 types) - Civil, criminal, specialized courts

  Category C: Contracts & Agreements (12 types) - Commercial, corporate, specialized
  Category D: Criminal Procedure (6 types) - FIRs, charges, warrants
  Category E: Corporate Governance (6 types) - Articles, resolutions, prospectuses
  Category F: Intellectual Property (6 types) - Patents, trademarks, copyrights
  Category G: Family Law (5 types) - Divorce, custody, adoption
  Category H: Tax & Revenue (4 types) - Assessments, rulings, appeals
  Category I: ADR Documents (3 types) - Arbitration, mediation
  Category J: Regulatory & Compliance (5 types) - EIAs, permits, certifications

   Chapter: I - Preliminary
      Section: 2(14)

    Chunk Text:
      "2. Definitions.
       (14) 'Capital asset' means property of any kind held by an assessee,
       whether or not connected with his business or profession, but does
       not include—
       (i) any stock-in-trade...
       (ii) movable property..."

    Size: 150-600 tokens per section/subsection
    Type: legislative_provision OR definition (if definitional section)

  APPROACH 2: Multi-Level Chunking (Recommended)
  ───────────────────────────────────────────────
  Level 1: Section Summary Chunk (for broad retrieval)
    - "Section 2(14) defines 'Capital asset' excluding stock-in-trade,
       personal effects under ₹3 lakhs, agricultural land, etc."
    - Size: 50-150 tokens
    - Type: definition

  Level 2: Full Section Chunk (for detailed retrieval)
    - Complete section text with all subsections
    - Size: 200-800 tokens
    - Type: legislative_provision

  Level 3: Proviso/Exception Chunks (for edge cases)
    - Extract "Provided that..." clauses separately
    - Size: 100-300 tokens
    - Type: exception_proviso

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Section level (NOT subsection, too granular)
  - Size: 200-600 tokens (statutes are dense)
  - Overlap: 0 tokens (sections are standalone)
  - Metadata: Act name, Part, Chapter, Section number, Amendment history

  ---
  B. Contracts & Agreements (Clause-Based Chunking)

  Challenge: Clauses reference each other, boilerplate vs custom clauses

  Recommended Strategy: Semantic Clause Chunking
  CHUNKING RULES:
  ─────────────────
  1. One clause = One chunk (clauses are atomic units)
  2. Classify clause type automatically:
     - obligation_clause: "Party A shall..."
     - condition_clause: "Upon the occurrence of..."
     - representation_warranty: "Party B represents that..."
     - remedy_clause: "In the event of breach..."
     - definition: "'Effective Date' means..."

  3. Prepend contract metadata:
     Contract: Software License Agreement
     Parties: Licensor (Company A) & Licensee (Company B)
     Date: 2024-01-15
     Clause: 5.3 - Termination Rights

  4. Extract cross-references:
     "...as defined in Clause 3.1..." → Create relationship to Clause 3.1

  5. De-duplicate boilerplate:
     - Generic clauses (force majeure, governing law) → Lower priority
     - Custom clauses → Higher priority

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Clause level (Article 5 → Clause 5.1, 5.2, 5.3)
  - Size: 100-500 tokens per clause
  - Overlap: 0 (clauses independent)
  - Type Detection: LLM-based classification into 4 contract chunk types

  ---
  C. Treaties & International Law (Protocol-Based + Multi-Lingual)

  Challenge: Multiple language versions, complex protocol structure

  Recommended Strategy: Parallel Text Chunking
  STRUCTURE:
  ──────────
  Paris Agreement on Climate Change
  ├── Preamble (chunk separately)
  ├── Article 1: Definitions (chunk by definition)
  ├── Article 2: Goals (chunk as treaty_article)
  ├── Article 3: Contributions (chunk with NDC context)
  ├── ...
  ├── Article 29: Entry into force (procedural)
  └── Annexes (chunk separately)

  MULTI-LINGUAL HANDLING:
  ───────────────────────
  Chunk ID: paris_agreement_art2_en
  Parallel Chunks:
    - paris_agreement_art2_fr (French authentic text)
    - paris_agreement_art2_es (Spanish authentic text)
    - paris_agreement_art2_zh (Chinese authentic text)

  Link via relationship: TRANSLATION_OF

  EMBEDDING STRATEGY:
  ───────────────────
  Option 1: Embed each language separately (BGE-M3 supports 100+ languages)
  Option 2: Embed English + store other languages as metadata

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Article level
  - Size: 150-600 tokens
  - Type: treaty_article (primary), definition (Article 1), international_principle

  ---
  D. Regulations & Rules (Rule-Based Chunking)

  Challenge: Dense sub-clauses, frequent amendments

  Recommended Strategy: Rule-Level with Amendment Tracking
  EXAMPLE: GDPR Article 6 (Lawfulness of processing)
  ─────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Chunk 1:
    Doc: GDPR (EU 2016/679)
    Article: 6
    Type: regulatory_rule

    "Processing shall be lawful only if at least one of the following applies:
     (a) the data subject has given consent...
     (b) processing is necessary for contract performance...
     (c) processing is necessary for compliance with legal obligation..."

    Size: 400 tokens

  Chunk 2 (Exception):
    Doc: GDPR (EU 2016/679)
    Article: 6(1)(f)
    Type: exception_proviso

    "Legitimate interests pursued by controller, except where overridden
     by interests of data subject, particularly if data subject is a child."

    Size: 150 tokens
    Amendment: None
    Related: Article 7 (Consent conditions)

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Rule/Sub-rule level
  - Size: 150-600 tokens
  - Overlap: 0
  - Amendment Tracking: Store version history in changelog

  ---
  E. Pleadings & Briefs (Argument-Based Chunking)

  Challenge: Persuasive narrative structure, heavy citations

  Recommended Strategy: Claim-Based Chunking
  STRUCTURE:
  ──────────
  Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus
  ├── Caption (metadata only, don't chunk)
  ├── Introduction (chunk as: arguments, 200 tokens)
  ├── Statement of Facts (chunk as: facts, 500-1000 tokens)
  ├── Legal Arguments
  │   ├── Argument I: Violation of Article 21
  │   │   ├── Sub-argument A: Arbitrary detention (chunk: arguments, 400 tokens)
  │   │   └── Sub-argument B: Precedent analysis (chunk: precedent_discussion, 300 tokens)
  │   ├── Argument II: Procedural irregularity
  │   │   └── (chunk as: procedural_history + arguments)
  │   └── Argument III: Constitutional remedy
  │       └── (chunk as: legal_analysis)
  └── Prayer/Relief Sought (metadata only)

  CITATION HANDLING:
  ──────────────────
  "As held in Maneka Gandhi v. Union of India (1978) 1 SCC 248, Article 21
   encompasses procedural fairness..."

  → Extract citation: Create CITES relationship to Maneka Gandhi case
  → Keep citation in chunk text (preserve context)

  Parameters:
  - Granularity: Argument level
  - Size: 300-800 tokens per argument
  - Type: arguments (primary), legal_analysis, precedent_discussion

  7. Neo4j Schema Expansion

  New Node Types Needed (Beyond Current 24):

  // Legislative nodes
  CREATE (s:Statute {statute_id, title, jurisdiction, enactment_date})
  CREATE (sec:Section {section_id, section_number, parent_statute})
  CREATE (a:Amendment {amendment_id, amendment_date, amending_act})

  // Contractual nodes
  CREATE (c:Contract {contract_id, parties, execution_date})
  CREATE (cl:Clause {clause_id, clause_number, clause_type})

  // International law nodes
  CREATE (t:Treaty {treaty_id, treaty_name, adoption_date})
  CREATE (p:Protocol {protocol_id, parent_treaty})

  // Regulatory nodes
  CREATE (r:Regulation {regulation_id, issuing_authority})

  New Relationships:

  // Legislative relationships
  (:Judgment)-[:INTERPRETS]->(:Section)
  (:Statute)-[:AMENDED_BY]->(:Amendment)
  (:Section)-[:PART_OF]->(:Statute)
  (:Regulation)-[:IMPLEMENTS]->(:Statute)

  // Contractual relationships
  (:Contract)-[:CONTAINS_CLAUSE]->(:Clause)
  (:Clause)-[:REFERENCES_CLAUSE]->(:Clause)
  (:Contract)-[:GOVERNED_BY]->(:Statute)

  // International relationships
  (:Treaty)-[:HAS_PROTOCOL]->(:Protocol)
  (:Judgment)-[:APPLIES_TREATY]->(:Treaty)
  (:Statute)-[:IMPLEMENTS_TREATY]->(:Treaty)

  9. Universal Chunking Pipeline (Revised)

  INPUT: Any legal document (judgment, statute, contract, treaty, etc.)
      ↓
  STEP 1: Document Classification
      - Detect document type using LLM + rule-based heuristics
      - Keywords: "JUDGMENT", "ACT", "AGREEMENT", "TREATY", etc.
      - Structure patterns: Numbered sections, clause structure, etc.
      ↓
  STEP 2: Extract Document-Specific Metadata
      - Judgments → court, judges, citation, date
      - Statutes → act name, chapter, section, amendment history
      - Contracts → parties, execution date, governing law
      - Treaties → treaty name, parties, adoption date, language
      ↓
  STEP 3: Apply Document-Specific Chunking Strategy
      ┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
      │ IF document_type == "judgment":         │
      │   → Use semantic section chunking       │
      │   → Chunk types: holding, reasoning, etc│
      │                                         │
      │ ELIF document_type == "statute":        │
      │   → Use hierarchical section chunking   │
      │   → Chunk types: legislative_provision  │
      │                                         │
      │ ELIF document_type == "contract":       │
      │   → Use clause-based chunking           │
      │   → Chunk types: obligation_clause, etc │
      │                                         │
      │ ELIF document_type == "treaty":         │
      │   → Use article-based chunking          │
      │   → Chunk types: treaty_article         │
      └─────────────────────────────────────────┘
      ↓
  STEP 4: Chunk Type Classification
      - LLM classifies each chunk into 16 universal types
      - Uses keywords + context + document type
      ↓
  STEP 5: Cross-Reference Extraction
      - Extract citations: "Section 22A", "Article 32", "Clause 5.3"
      - Create Neo4j relationships: CITES, REFERENCES, INTERPRETS
      ↓
  STEP 6: Metadata Enrichment & Embedding
      - Prepend context: doc type + metadata + chunk type
      - Generate embeddings (BGE-M3)
      - Calculate trust_score, confidence_score
      ↓
  OUTPUT: Universal chunks ready for Neo4j + Weaviate indexing

  ---
  10. Retrieval Strategy Adaptations

  Query → Document Type Routing

  QUERY ANALYSIS:
  ───────────────
  "What is the penalty for data breach?"
  → Document types: statutes (GDPR), regulations (data protection rules)
  → Chunk types: regulatory_rule, remedy_clause
  → Boost: legislative_provision chunks with "penalty", "fine", "sanction"

  "Show me force majeure clauses"
  → Document types: contracts
  → Chunk types: condition_clause
  → Boost: contract chunks with keywords "force majeure", "act of god"

  "Cases interpreting Article 21"
  → Document types: judgments
  → Chunk types: statute_interpretation, legal_analysis
  → Boost: chunks with "Article 21" + "held" + "Constitution"

  "Treaty obligations on climate finance"
  → Document types: treaties
  → Chunk types: treaty_article, obligation_clause
  → Boost: treaty chunks with "climate", "finance", "developed countries"

  Multi-Document Retrieval Pipeline

  STAGE 1: Identify Relevant Document Types
      Query: "GDPR consent requirements in employment contracts"
      → Document types: regulations (GDPR) + contracts (employment)
      ↓
  STAGE 2: Parallel Retrieval Across Document Types
      Path A: Search regulations for "consent" → regulatory_rule chunks
      Path B: Search contracts for "consent" → obligation_clause chunks
      Path C: Search judgments for "GDPR employment consent" → legal_analysis
      ↓
  STAGE 3: Cross-Document Fusion
      - Merge results using RRF
      - Boost chunks with cross-references (contract referencing GDPR)
      - Rank by: similarity (0.4) + trust_score (0.3) + document_type_relevance (0.3)
      ↓
  OUTPUT: Top 10 chunks across multiple document types

  1. Core Procedural Documents (~70 types missing)

  - Civil procedure: Summons, answers, interrogatories, depositions, subpoenas, default judgments, class certifications
  - Criminal procedure: Informations, arraignments, plea agreements, presentence reports, parole hearings, pardons, expungements
  - Appellate procedure: Appeals, briefs, amicus curiae, certiorari petitions, rehearing petitions

  2. Financial Regulation (~30 types missing)

  - Securities: Form S-1, 10-K, 10-Q, 8-K, proxy statements, Schedule 13D, Form 4, Regulation D, SEC enforcement
  - Banking: Bank charters, merger approvals, FDIC insurance, examination reports, cease and desist orders, CTRs

  3. Tax Administration (~15 types missing)

  - Private letter rulings, revenue rulings, technical advice memoranda, offers in compromise, innocent spouse relief, tax liens/levies

  4. Intellectual Property (~15 types missing)

  - Utility models, plant variety rights, geographical indications, database rights, work-for-hire agreements, moral rights waivers

  5. Commercial Law (~9 types missing)

  - Letters of credit variants, bills of exchange, promissory notes, negotiable instruments, warehouse receipts

  6. International Trade (~13 types missing)

  - Certificates of origin, customs declarations, ATA carnets, anti-dumping duties, rules of origin determinations

  7. Social Services (~20 types missing)

  - Child welfare: Foster care, termination of parental rights, juvenile delinquency
  - Disability: IEPs, Section 504 plans, ADA accommodations
  - Elder law: Nursing home agreements, Medicare appeals

  8. Land Use & Zoning (~13 types missing)

  - Special use permits, conditional use permits, subdivision approvals, wetlands permits, historic designations

  9. Professional Licensing (~10 types missing)

  - Dental, pharmacy, veterinary, psychology, social work, teaching, contractor boards

  10. Additional Gaps:

  - Electoral law (10 types)
  - Animal law (10 types)
  - Entertainment law details (12 types)
  - Government documents (20 types)
  - Post-2020 emerging regulations (13 types)

     │ PHASE 3: CHUNKING STRATEGIES BY DOCUMENT TYPE                                                                                                                                 │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Strategy Matrix (910 document types mapped to chunking approaches)                                                                                                            │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Hierarchical Chunking (250 types):                                                                                                                                            │
     │ - Statutes, regulations, codes                                                                                                                                                │
     │ - Chunk by: Section → Subsection → Paragraph                                                                                                                                  │
     │ - Size: 200-600 tokens                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ - Overlap: 0 (sections are atomic)                                                                                                                                            │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Semantic Chunking (180 types):                                                                                                                                                │
     │ - Judgments, opinions, legal analysis                                                                                                                                         │
     │ - Chunk by: Topic/legal issue boundaries                                                                                                                                      │
     │ - Size: 600-800 tokens                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ - Overlap: 150 tokens (25%)                                                                                                                                                   │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Clause-Based Chunking (200 types):                                                                                                                                            │
     │ - Contracts, agreements                                                                                                                                                       │
     │ - Chunk by: Individual clauses                                                                                                                                                │
     │ - Size: 100-500 tokens                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ - Overlap: 0 (clauses are independent)                                                                                                                                        │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Procedural Chunking (120 types):                                                                                                                                              │
     │ - Pleadings, motions, briefs                                                                                                                                                  │
     │ - Chunk by: Argument/claim units                                                                                                                                              │
     │ - Size: 400-700 tokens                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ - Overlap: 100 tokens                                                                                                                                                         │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Financial/Structured Chunking (80 types):                                                                                                                                     │
     │ - Securities filings, financial reports                                                                                                                                       │
     │ - Chunk by: Disclosure sections + extract tables                                                                                                                              │
     │ - Size: 500-1000 tokens                                                                                                                                                       │
     │ - Preserve numerical data as structured JSON                                                                                                                                  │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Technical Chunking (60 types):                                                                                                                                                │
     │ - Patents, technical reports                                                                                                                                                  │
     │ - Chunk by: Claims (atomic) + descriptions (semantic)                                                                                                                         │
     │ - Size: Claims (50-500), Descriptions (800-1000)                                                                                                                              │
     │ - Overlap: 250 tokens for descriptions                                                                                                                                        │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │
     │ Hybrid Chunking (20 types):                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ - Complex multi-part documents                                                                                                                                                │
     │ - Multi-level: Summary → Sections → Details                                                                                                                                   │
     │ - Adaptive sizing based on content density                                                                                                                                    │
     │                                                                                                                                                                               │

  CRITICAL VERIFICATION: Is This Truly #1 with ZERO Gaps?

  Comparison with Industry Leaders

  1. Westlaw (Thomson Reuters) - Estimated 40,000+ unique document collections
  - Our 910 types = document TYPE taxonomy, not individual documents
  - Westlaw's collections include billions of documents across ~500-600 distinct document TYPES
  - Coverage comparison: ~90-95% of Westlaw's document types

  2. LexisNexis - Similar scale to Westlaw
  - Estimated 400-500 distinct document types
  - Coverage comparison: ~95% of LexisNexis types

  - Estimated 300-400 document types
  - Coverage comparison: ~98% of Bloomberg Law types

  - Coverage comparison: ~99% of their types

     │ # Query in English, retrieve documents in any language                                                                                                 │
     │ query = "GDPR data breach notification requirements"                                                                                                   │

     │ ---                                                                                                                                                    │
     │ COMPLETE SYSTEM ARCHITECTURE                                                                                                                           │
     │                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ Retrieval Pipeline                                                                                                                                     │
     │                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ 1. User Query → Query Understanding                                                                                                                    │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 2. Query Expansion + Disambiguation                                                                                                                    │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 3. Parallel Retrieval:                                                                                                                                 │
     │    - Vector Search (Weaviate/BGE-M3) → Top 100                                                                                                         │
     │    - BM25 Keyword Search → Top 100                                                                                                                     │
     │    - Neo4j Graph Traversal → Top 50                                                                                                                    │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 4. RRF Fusion → Top 150                                                                                                                                │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 5. Cross-Encoder Reranking (Cohere/Voyage) → Top 50                                                                                                    │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 6. Trust-Weighted Scoring:                                                                                                                             │
     │    score = 0.35*similarity + 0.30*citation_strength +                                                                                                  │
     │            0.20*court_authority + 0.15*recency                                                                                                         │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 7. Final Top 20 Results                                                                                                                                │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 8. For Each Result:                                                                                                                                    │
     │    - Citation strength score                                                                                                                           │
     │    - Treatment history                                                                                                                                 │
     │    - Judge/case analytics                                                                                                                              │
     │    - Related documents                                                                                                                                 │
     │    - Cross-references                                                                                                                                  │
     │    ↓                                                                                                                                                   │
     │ 9. Return via API to Your Agentic AI System                                                                                                            │
     │                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ Your Agentic AI Integration                                                                                                                            │
     │                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ # Your agentic system calls our retriever                                                                                                              │
     │ retrieval_results = legal_retriever_api.search(                                                                                                        │
     │     query="Article 21 privacy rights",                                                                                                                 │
     │     top_k=20                                                                                                                                           │
     │ )                                                                                                                                                      │
     │                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ # You get high-quality chunks with metadata                                                                                                            │
     │ for result in retrieval_results:                                                                                                                       │
     │     chunk = result["text"]              # 600-800 token chunk                                                                                          │
     │     citation = result["citation"]        # Formatted citation                                                                                          │
     │     strength = result["citation_score"]  # 0-1 score                                                                                                   │
     │     analytics = result["judge_data"]     # Win rates, patterns                                                                                         │
     │     related = result["related_docs"]     # Cross-references                                                                                            │
     │                                                                                                                                                        │
     │ # Your agentic AI uses this for generation                                                                                                             │
     │ answer = your_llm.generate(                                                                                                                            │
     │     prompt=f"Using these legal sources: {retrieval_results}\n\nAnswer: {query}",                                                                       │
     │     citations=True                                                                                                                                     │
     │ )                                                                                                                                                      │
     │                                                                                                                                                        │

     │ Technology: FastAPI (Python 3.11)                                                                                                         │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │ Tasks:                                                                                                                                    │
     │ 1. API Structure                                                                                                                          │
     │ # src/api/main.py                                                                                                                         │
     │ from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException                                                                                                │
     │ from pydantic import BaseModel                                                                                                            │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │ app = FastAPI(title="Legal Retriever API", version="1.0.0")                                                                               │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │ class SearchRequest(BaseModel):                                                                                                           │
     │     query: str                                                                                                                            │
     │     jurisdiction: Optional[str]                                                                                                           │
     │     document_types: Optional[List[str]]                                                                                                   │
     │     date_range: Optional[DateRange]                                                                                                       │
     │     limit: int = 20                                                                                                                       │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │ @app.post("/api/v1/search")                                                                                                               │
     │ async def search(request: SearchRequest):                                                                                                 │
     │     # Vector search                                                                                                                       │
     │     vector_results = await vector_search(request)                                                                                         │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │     # BM25 search                                                                                                                         │
     │     bm25_results = await bm25_search(request)                                                                                             │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │     # Merge using RRF                                                                                                                     │
     │     merged_results = reciprocal_rank_fusion(vector_results, bm25_results)                                                                 │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │     return {"results": merged_results}                                                                                                    │
     │ 2. Hybrid Search Implementation                                                                                                           │
     │ # src/search/hybrid.py                                                                                                                    │
     │ def reciprocal_rank_fusion(list1, list2, k=60):                                                                                           │
     │     """                                                                                                                                   │
     │     RRF formula: score = sum(1 / (k + rank_i))                                                                                            │
     │     """                                                                                                                                   │
     │     scores = defaultdict(float)                                                                                                           │
     │     for rank, doc in enumerate(list1):                                                                                                    │
     │         scores[doc.id] += 1 / (k + rank + 1)                                                                                              │
     │     for rank, doc in enumerate(list2):                                                                                                    │
     │         scores[doc.id] += 1 / (k + rank + 1)                                                                                              │
     │                                                                                                                                           │
     │     return sorted(scores.items(), key=lambda x: x[1], reverse=True)                                                                       │
     │ 3. Authentication & Rate Limiting                                                                                                         │

     │   - Rate limiting (100 requests/minute per key)                                                                                           │
     │   - Usage tracking                                                                                                                        │
